song?&quot;,&quot;contributors_count&quot;:2,&quot;created_at&quot;:1473542695,&quot;default_key&quot;:&quot;artist_comment&quot;,&quot;has_voters&quot;:false,&quot;id&quot;:18276,&quot;pin_order&quot;:65536.0,&quot;state&quot;:&quot;pinned&quot;,&quot;url&quot;:&quot;https://genius.com/Papa-roach-last-resort-lyrics/questions/18276&quot;,&quot;votes_total&quot;:0,&quot;current_user_metadata&quot;:{&quot;permissions&quot;:[],&quot;excluded_permissions&quot;:[&quot;vote&quot;,&quot;add_answer&quot;,&quot;update_answer_source&quot;,&quot;edit&quot;,&quot;archive&quot;,&quot;pin&quot;,&quot;unpin&quot;,&quot;move&quot;,&quot;add_verified_answer&quot;],&quot;iq_by_action&quot;:{},&quot;interactions&quot;:{&quot;vote&quot;:null}},&quot;answer&quot;:{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;answer&quot;,&quot;body&quot;:{&quot;html&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;http://www.songfacts.com/blog/interviews/tobin_esperance_of_papa_roach/\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;Tobin Esperance went into detail&lt;/a&gt; regarding the influences that inspired this hit in 2011:&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Well, of course at the time we were listening to a lot of Wu Tang Clan, a lot of hip-hop, and a lot of Fugees and a lot of East Coast hip-hop…I was playing something on piano and Jacoby came in and started scatting over it. And we just did our typical mixing of a funky kind of hip-hop groove with a punk rock chorus. We did it over and over again, and Jacoby put his lyrics to it, and the song just morphed into what it is now. No one ever thought it was going to be a huge, huge hit, but I guess you never expect anything, really, when you’re first starting out.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;http://www.mtv.com/news/1122601/fans-finding-hope-in-papa-roachs-last-resort/\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;Jacoby Shaddix&lt;/a&gt; talked about the original inspiration for the song’s lyrics:&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;I was just putting it out on the table, you know, this is what this guy went through, and this is how he felt. It has a positive edge to it, as far as like, ‘Don’t succumb to it. Keep yourself afloat. With these problems in your life, find a friend you can confide in.’&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;He also told &lt;a href=\&quot;http://www.songfacts.com/blog/interviews/jacoby_shaddix_of_papa_roach/\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener nofollow\&quot;&gt;&lt;em&gt;SongMeanings&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;blockquote&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;That song was a cry for help. That song was about one of my best friends, and then 12-13 years later, that song was about me. I found myself in that place, where I was like, “I can’t go on this way. I can’t do it anymore.”&lt;/p&gt;\n\n&lt;p&gt;It’s awesome when your cry for help gets answered. My band has had my back over these years, and my friends and my family. That song is timeless and it connects with who we are today and what we do today in a major way.&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;/blockquote&gt;&quot;,&quot;markdown&quot;:&quot;[Tobin Esperance went into detail](http://www.songfacts.com/blog/interviews/tobin_esperance_of_papa_roach/) regarding the influences that inspired this hit in 2011:\n\n&gt;Well, of course at the time we were listening to a lot of Wu Tang Clan, a lot of hip-hop, and a lot of Fugees and a lot of East Coast hip-hop...I was playing something on piano and Jacoby came in and started scatting over it. And we just did our typical mixing of a funky kind of hip-hop groove with a punk rock chorus. We did it over and over again, and Jacoby put his lyrics to it, and the song just morphed into what it is now. No one ever thought it was going to be a huge, huge hit, but I guess you never expect anything, really, when you&#39;re first starting out.\n\n[Jacoby Shaddix](http://www.mtv.com/news/1122601/fans-finding-hope-in-papa-roachs-last-resort/) talked about the original inspiration for the song&#39;s lyrics:\n\n&gt;I was just putting it out on the table, you know, this is what this guy went through, and this is how he felt. It has a positive edge to it, as far as like, ‘Don’t succumb to it. Keep yourself afloat. With these problems in your life, find a friend you can confide in.’\n\nHe also told [*SongMeanings*](http://www.songfacts.com/blog/interviews/jacoby_shaddix_of_papa_roach/)\n&gt;That song was a cry for help. That song was about one of my best friends, and then 12-13 years later, that song was about me. I found myself in that place, where I was like, \&quot;I can&#39;t go on this way. I can&#39;t do it anymore.\&quot; \n\n&gt;It&#39;s awesome when your cry for help gets answered. My band has had my back over these years, and my friends and my family. That song is timeless and it connects with who we are today and what we do today in a major way.&quot;},&quot;created_at&quot;:1473542695,&quot;editorial_state&quot;:&quot;normal&quot;,&quot;has_voters&quot;:true,&quot;id&quot;:3707,&quot;votes_total&quot;:8,&quot;current_user_metadata&quot;:{&quot;permissions&quot;:[],&quot;excluded_permissions&quot;:[&quot;vote&quot;,&quot;edit&quot;,&quot;destroy&quot;],&quot;interactions&quot;:{&quot;vote&quot;:null}},&quot;answer_source&quot;:null,&quot;authors&quot;:[{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;user_attribution&quot;,&quot;attribution&quot;:0.6723549488054608,&quot;pinned_role&quot;:null,&quot;user&quot;:{&quot;_type&quot;:&quot;user&quot;,&quot;about_me_summary&quot;:&quot;I’m a product of my environment.\n\nI annotate mostly songs from my childhood, or at least songs from bands that were popular from my childhood. does not go with me, I’m addicted to the lyrics that spill one’s heart away.\n\nPreface: FGV\n\nIf you ever make your way to The City of Eternal Spring you’ll probably see FGV, gazing at the mountains and playing his Epiphone Les Paul Traditional Pro or his Ibanez Zebrawood to monumental rock pieces. As time goes by he’ll probably leave to learn how to achieve total world domination, constructing robots programmed with artificial intelligence. He often times clears his agenda to illuminate the masses with rational, reflective, and ingenious lyric deconstructions and uses Genius as his medium to manifest his knowledge.\n\n\n\nHey! I’m Federico García Vélez [FGV], a Colombian music lover, mechatronic engineer, guitarist, and songwriter. I’m in love with searching the meaning behind profound music, art, and literature. Rock, Alternative, Punk, and Metal are powerful forces that drive my soul; adrenaline filled guitar riffs with deep messages make my blood rush while deep and heartfelt ballads keep me up at night.\n\nIf I have come to delete your tate, it’s nothing personal, shoot me a message and I’ll gladly explain why it was rejected. If you have any other questions about Genius or want to become an editor, hit me up, and I’ll try to show you the means of the yellow square!\n\nTambién, como pueden ver que soy de Colombia, hablo Español! This song is about suicide, as Coby said it was about a close friend who was having issues in several interviews, including one with MTV back in 2000.\n\nI was just putting it out on the table, you know, this is what this guy went through, and this is how he felt. It has a positive edge to it, as far as like, ‘Don’t succumb to it. Keep yourself afloat. With these problems in your life, find a friend you can confide in.’\n\nYears later, he relates to it on a personal level, because of his own struggle with sobriety, which led to his own struggle with suicide, as chronicled in the song “Before I Die.”&quot;,&quot;markdown&quot;:&quot;These lyrics are intensely disturbing, allowing you to relate to the deep pain being expressed. <div class="text_label text_label--gray">More on Genius</div>
<a href="https://genius.com/a/papa-roach-trolled-donald-trump-with-the-lyrics-to-their-2000-hit-last-resort" class="recirculated_content">
<div class="recirculated_content-image"></div>
<div class="recirculated_content-info">
<div class="recirculated_content-title">Papa Roach Trolled Donald Trump With The Lyrics To Their 2000 Hit “Last Resort”</div>
</div>
</a>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="column_layout-column_span column_layout-column_span--secondary u-top_margin column_layout-flex_column">
<div class="column_layout-column_span-initial_content">
<div class="dfp_unit u-x_large_bottom_margin dfp_unit--in_read">
<div
style="
width: 300px;
height: 250px;
"
></div>
</div>


<div class="annotation_label">
<h3 class="u-inline">
About “Last Resort”
</h3>
</div>
<div class="rich_text_formatting">
<p>This song is about the cutting and <a href="http://www.mtv.com/news/1122601/fans-finding-hope-in-papa-roachs-last-resort/" rel="noopener nofollow">suicidal thoughts</a> of one of the band’s friends.</p>

<p>Papa Roach’s “Last Resort” held its ground on the Billboard Hot 100 for <a href="http://www.billboard.com/artist/277209/papa+roach/chart" rel="noopener nofollow">three straight months</a>, making it one of the most famous rock songs released that year. With a slower tempo drum beat contrasted with a quick, driving melody, the instrumental composition almost sounds like a hip-hop song.</p>
</div>
<div class="song_metadata u-xx_large_bottom_margin"></div>
</div>

<div class="column_layout-column_span-initial_content">
<div initial-content-for="question_list">
<ul>
<li class="question question--bottom_border ">
<div class="u-bottom_margin">
<h3 class="annotation_label">What have the artists said about the song?</h3>
</div>
<div class="rich_text_formatting rich_text_formatting--no_vertical_margins">
<p><a href="http://www.songfacts.com/blog/interviews/tobin_esperance_of_papa_roach/" rel="noopener nofollow">Tobin Esperance went into detail</a> regarding the influences that inspired this hit in 2011:</p>

<blockquote><p>Well, of course at the time we were listening to a lot of Wu Tang Clan, a lot of hip-hop, and a lot of Fugees and a lot of East Coast hip-hop…I was playing something on piano and Jacoby came in and started scatting over it. And we just did our typical mixing of a funky kind of hip-hop groove with a punk rock chorus. We did it over and over again, and Jacoby put his lyrics to it, and the song just morphed into what it is now. No one ever thought it was going to be a huge, huge hit, but I guess you never expect anything, really, when you’re first starting out.</p></blockquote>

<p><a href="http://www.mtv.com/news/1122601/fans-finding-hope-in-papa-roachs-last-resort/" rel="noopener nofollow">Jacoby Shaddix</a> talked about the original inspiration for the song’s lyrics:</p>

<blockquote><p>I was just putting it out on the table, you know, this is what this guy went through, and this is how he felt. It has a positive edge to it, as far as like, ‘Don’t succumb to it. Keep yourself afloat. With these problems in your life, find a friend you can confide in.’</p></blockquote>

<p>He also told <a href="http://www.songfacts.com/blog/interviews/jacoby_shaddix_of_papa_roach/" rel="noopener nofollow"><em>SongMeanings</em></a></p>

<blockquote>
<p>That song was a cry for help. That song was about one of my best friends, and then 12-13 years later, that song was about me. I found myself in that place, where I was like, “I can’t go on this way. I can’t do it anymore.”</p>

<p>It’s awesome when your cry for help gets answered. My band has had my back over these years, and my friends and my family. That song is timeless and it connects with who we are today and what we do today in a major way.</p>
</blockquote>
</div>


</li>

</ul>
</div>
